  > enny L.   > er's unsworn allegations - Curated audio recordings (no foundation) - Hearsay statements (no exception)  #### Pattern 3: Stigmatizing Language  Judge McNeill used stigmatizing language directed only at Father: - Called Father "crazy" on the record - Called Father "liar" on the record - Made assumpti

- **McNeill imposed**
  > ental health without diagnostic basis - Made no similar statements about Mother  #### Pattern 4: Procedural Barriers to Father's Participation  Judge McNeill imposed barriers to Father's access to the court: - Stated on record: "Do not file any more. I will not look at it." - Imposed $250 filing fee

- **McNeill treated**
  > ent time - Muted Father during remote hearings - Refused to consider Father's written objections  #### Pattern 5: Unequal Treatment of Parties  Judge McNeill treated Father and Mother unequally: - Sanctioned Father for disputed communication - Did not sanction Mother for documented withholding - Imp

- **McNeill called**
  > dmitted unauthenticated evidence favorable to Mother while excluding authenticated evidence favorable to Father.  3. **Stigmatizing language.** Judge McNeill called Father "crazy" and "liar" on the record, demonstrating bias and prejudgment.  4. **Procedural barriers.** Judge McNeill imposed barrier

  > r children. Meyer v. Nebraska, 262 US 390 (1923); Pierce v. Society of Sisters, 268 US 510 (1925); Troxel v. Granville, 530 US 57 (2000). - **The Court further held**
  > the care, custody, and control of their children is perhaps the oldest of the fundamental liberty interests recognized by this Court." 530 US at 65. The Court further held that this interest is protected by the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.  #### B. The Trial Court Deprived Father
